<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Forest</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Dense collection of trees covering a relatively large area</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about a community of trees. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Forest_(disambiguation)" title="Forest (disambiguation)">Forest (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For broader coverage of this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Plant_community" title="Plant community">Plant community</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG/330px-Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG/495px-Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG/660px-Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinophyta" title="Pinophyta">conifer forest</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Alps" title="Swiss Alps">Swiss Alps</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swiss_National_Park" title="Swiss National Park">National Park</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>A <b>forest</b> is an area of land dominated by <a href="/wiki/Tree" title="Tree">trees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Hundreds of definitions of forest are used throughout the world, incorporating factors such as tree density, tree height, land use, legal standing, and ecological function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbd_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbd-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unep_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-unep-4">[4]</a></sup> The United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO) defines a forest as, "Land spanning more than 0.5 hectares with trees higher than 5 meters and a <a href="/wiki/Canopy_(biology)" title="Canopy (biology)">canopy</a> cover of more than 10 percent, or trees able to reach these thresholds <i>in situ</i>. It does not include land that is predominantly under agricultural or urban use."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Using this definition, <i><a href="/wiki/Global_Forest_Resources_Assessment_(FRA)" title="Global Forest Resources Assessment (FRA)">Global Forest Resources Assessment</a> 2020</i> (FRA 2020) found that forests covered 4.06 billion hectares (10.0 billion acres; 40.6 million square kilometres; 15.7 million square miles), or approximately 31 percent of the world's land area in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Forests are the predominant terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a> of Earth, and are found around the globe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yude_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-yude-7">[7]</a></sup> More than half of the world's forests are found in only five countries (Brazil, Canada, China, Russia, and the United States). The largest share of forests (45 percent) are in the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical latitudes</a>, followed by those in the <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">boreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temperate_rainforest" title="Temperate rainforest">temperate</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropic" title="Subtropic">subtropic</a> domains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>Forests account for 75% of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_primary_production" title="Gross primary production">gross primary production</a> of the Earth's <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a>, and contain 80% of the Earth's plant <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a>. <a href="/wiki/Primary_production#Gross_primary_production_and_net_primary_production" title="Primary production">Net primary production</a> is estimated at 21.9 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigatonne" title="Gigatonne">gigatonnes</a> of biomass per year for <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical forests</a>, 8.1 for <a href="/wiki/Temperate_forest" title="Temperate forest">temperate forests</a>, and 2.6 for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boreal_forest" title="Boreal forest">boreal forests</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yude_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-yude-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Forests at different latitudes and elevations, and with different precipitation and <a href="/wiki/Evapotranspiration" title="Evapotranspiration">evapotranspiration</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> form distinctly different <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biomes</a>: boreal forests around the North Pole, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">tropical moist forests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_dry_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical dry broadleaf forests">tropical dry forests</a> around the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">Equator</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Temperate_forest" title="Temperate forest">temperate forests</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Middle_latitudes" title="Middle latitudes">middle latitudes</a>. Areas at higher elevations tend to support forests similar to those at higher latitudes, and the amount of precipitation also affects forest composition.
</p><p>Almost half the forest area (49 percent) is relatively intact, while 9 percent is found in fragments with little or no connectivity. Tropical rainforests and boreal coniferous forests are the least fragmented, whereas subtropical dry forests and temperate oceanic forests are among the most fragmented. Roughly 80 percent of the world's forest area is found in patches larger than 1 million hectares (2.5 million acres). The remaining 20 percent is located in more than 34 million patches around the world – the vast majority less than 1,000 hectares (2,500 acres) in size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>Human society and forests influence each other in both positive and negative ways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Forests provide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a> to humans and serve as tourist attractions. Forests can also affect people's health. Human activities, including unsustainable use of forest resources, can negatively affect forest ecosystems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p>
